/></a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Humacao</b> (<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1177148991">.mw-parser-output .IPA-label-small{font-size:85%}.mw-parser-output .references .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .infobox .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .navbox .IPA-label-small{font-size:100%}</style><span class="IPA-label IPA-label-small">Spanish pronunciation:</span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="es-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">&#91;uma\xcb\x88kao&#93;</a></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/Humacao_barrio-pueblo" title="Humacao barrio-pueblo">city</a> and <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Municipalities of Puerto Rico">municipality</a> in <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> located in the eastern coast of the island, north of <a href="/wiki/Yabucoa,_Puerto_Rico" title="Yabucoa, Puerto Rico">Yabucoa</a>; south of <a href="/wiki/Naguabo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Naguabo, Puerto Rico">Naguabo</a>; east of <a href="/wiki/Las_Piedras,_Puerto_Rico" title="Las Piedras, Puerto Rico">Las Piedras</a>; and west of <a href="/wiki/Vieques,_Puerto_Rico" title="Vieques, Puerto Rico">Vieques Passage</a>. Humacao is spread over 12 barrios and <a href="/wiki/Humacao_barrio-pueblo" title="Humacao barrio-pueblo">Humacao Pueblo</a> (the downtown area and the administrative center of the city). It is part of the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan-Caguas-Guaynabo_Metropolitan_Statistical_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="San Juan-Caguas-Guaynabo Metropolitan Statistical Area">San Juan-Caguas-Guaynabo Metropolitan Statistical Area</a>.\n</p>\n<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Humacao,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Statue_of_Cacique_Jumacao_(Humacao,_Puerto_Rico).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Statue_of_Cacique_Jumacao_%28Humacao%2C_Puerto_Rico%29.jpg/150px-Statue_of_Cacique_Jumacao_%28Humacao%2C_Puerto_Rico%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="226" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Statue_of_Cacique_Jumacao_%28Humacao%2C_Puerto_Rico%29.jpg/225px-Statue_of_Cacique_Jumacao_%28Humacao%2C_Puerto_Rico%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e0/Statue_of_Cacique_Jumacao_%28Humacao%2C_Puerto_Rico%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="266" data-file-height="400" /></a><figcaption>Statue of Cacique Jumacao</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The region of what is now Humacao belonged to the <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Ta\xc3\xadno people">Ta\xc3\xadno</a> region of Humaka, which covered a portion of the southeast coast of Puerto Rico.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The region was led by cacique <a href="/wiki/Jumacao" title="Jumacao">Jumacao</a> (also referred to as "Macao").<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The Ta\xc3\xadno settlement was located on the shores of what is called now the <a href="/wiki/Humacao_River" title="Humacao River">Humacao River</a>. It is believed that the Ta\xc3\xadno chief Jumacao was the first "cacique" to learn to read and write in Spanish, since he wrote a letter to the <a href="/wiki/King_of_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="King of Spain">King of Spain</a> <a href="/wiki/Charles_I_of_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Charles I of Spain">Charles I</a> complaining about how the <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Governor of Puerto Rico">Governor of the island</a> wasn\'t complying with their peace agreement. In the letter, Jumacao argued that their people were virtually prisoners of Spain. It is said that King Charles was so moved by the letter that he ordered the Governor to obey the terms of the treaty.<sup id="cite_ref-linktopr_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-linktopr-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AA_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AA-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Self-published_sources" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag may rely on a self-published source. (January 2018)">self-published source</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>During the early 16th century, the region was populated by <a href="/wiki/Cattle_ranching" class="mw-redirect" title="Cattle ranching">cattle ranchers</a>. However, since most of them officially resided in <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a>, a settlement was never officially organized. At the beginning of the 18th century, specifically around 1721\xe2\x80\x931722, the first official settlement was constituted in the area. Most of the residents at the time were immigrants from the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a>, but due to attacks from <a href="/wiki/Island_Caribs" class="mw-redirect" title="Island Caribs">Caribs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Piracy_in_the_Caribbean" title="Piracy in the Caribbean">pirates</a>, and other settlers, some of them moved farther into the island in what is now <a href="/wiki/Las_Piedras,_Puerto_Rico" title="Las Piedras, Puerto Rico">Las Piedras</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-enciclopediapr_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-enciclopediapr-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Still, some settlers remained and by 1776, historian <a href="/wiki/Fray_%C3%8D%C3%B1igo_Abbad_y_Lasierra" title="Fray \xc3\x8d\xc3\xb1igo Abbad y Lasierra">Fray \xc3\x8d\xc3\xb1igo Abbad y Lasierra</a> visited the area and wrote about the population there. By 1793, the church was recognized as parish and the settlement was officially recognized as town.<sup id="cite_ref-linktopr_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-linktopr-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>By 1894, Humacao was recognized as a city. Due to its thriving population, buildings and structures like a hospital, a theater, and a prison were built in the city. In 1899, after the United States invasion of the island as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War">Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War</a>, the municipality of <a href="/wiki/Las_Piedras,_Puerto_Rico" title="Las Piedras, Puerto Rico">Las Piedras</a> was annexed to Humacao. This lasted until 1914, when the <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Assembly_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Legislative Assembly of Puerto Rico">Legislative Assembly of Puerto Rico</a> voted on splitting both towns again.<sup id="cite_ref-enciclopediapr_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-enciclopediapr-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Puerto Rico was ceded by <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> in the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War">Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War</a> under the terms of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_of_1898" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Paris of 1898">Treaty of Paris of 1898</a> and became a territory of the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. In 1899, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_War" title="United States Department of War">United States Department of War</a> conducted a <a href="/wiki/Census" title="Census">census</a> of Puerto Rico finding that the population of Humacao was 14,313.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Humacao was led by mayor <a href="/wiki/Marcelo_Trujillo_Panisse" class="mw-redirect" title="Marcelo Trujillo Panisse">Marcelo Trujillo Panisse</a> for over a decade. A basketball star in his early years, Trujillo has pushed for the development of infrastructure facilities for sports and the fine arts in the city. In March 2008, a new <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholic</a> diocese was established as the <a href="/wiki/Fajardo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Fajardo, Puerto Rico">Fajardo</a>-Humacao diocese. Its first bishop is Monsignor <a href="/wiki/Eusebio_Ramos_Morales" title="Eusebio Ramos Morales">Eusebio \'Chebito\' Ramos Morales</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Maunabo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Maunabo, Puerto Rico">maunabe\xc3\xb1o</a> who was rector of the Humacao\'s main parish in the 1990s.\n</p><p>In 2019, Luis Raul Sanchez became interim mayor of Humacao after Marcelo Trujillo Panisse died in September 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-2019_mayor_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2019_mayor-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>On September 20, 2017 <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a> struck Puerto Rico.  Punta Santiago in Humacao saw a six-foot storm surge. The hurricane caused destruction of homes and infrastructure.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Geography">Geography</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Humacao,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Humacao is located in the southeast coast of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>. It is bordered by the municipalities of <a href="/wiki/Naguabo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Naguabo, Puerto Rico">Naguabo</a> to the north, <a href="/wiki/Yabucoa,_Puerto_Rico" title="Yabucoa, Puerto Rico">Yabucoa</a> to the south, and <a href="/wiki/Las_Piedras,_Puerto_Rico" title="Las Piedras, Puerto Rico">Las Piedras</a> to the west. The Atlantic Ocean borders the city in the east. Humacao is located in the region of the Eastern Coastal Plains, with most of its territory being flat. There are minor elevations to the southwest, like Candelero Hill, and northwest, like Mab\xc3\xba. Humacao\'s territory covers 45 square miles (117&#160;km<sup>2</sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-linktopr_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-linktopr-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Two islands belong to Humacao: <a href="/wiki/Cayo_Santiago" title="Cayo Santiago">Cayo Santiago</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cayo_Batata" title="Cayo Batata">Cayo Batata</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Water_features">Water features</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Humacao,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Water features"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Humacao\'s hydrographic system consists of many rivers and creeks like <a href="/wiki/Humacao_River" title="Humacao River">Humacao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anton_Ruiz_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Anton Ruiz River">Ant\xc3\xb3n Ru\xc3\xadz</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Candelero_River" title="Candelero River">Candelero</a>. Some of its creeks are Frontera, Mariana, and Del Obispo, among many others.<sup id="cite_ref-linktopr_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-linktopr-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2019, updated flood zone maps show that Humacao is extremely vulnerable to flooding, along with <a href="/wiki/Toa_Baja,_Puerto_Rico" title="Toa Baja, Puerto Rico">Toa Baja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rinc%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico" title="Rinc\xc3\xb3n, Puerto Rico">Rinc\xc3\xb3n</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barceloneta,_Puerto_Rico" title="Barceloneta, Puerto Rico">Barceloneta</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Corozal,_Puerto_Rico" title="Corozal, Puerto Rico">Corozal</a>. Located where most cyclones enter the island, Humacao is one of the most vulnerable areas of Puerto Rico.<sup id="cite_ref-Le\xc3\xb3n_END_Flood_Zones_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Le\xc3\xb3n_END_Flood_Zones-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Humacao was working on flood mitigation plans and shared that its barrios located on the coast; <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3n_Ru%C3%ADz" title="Ant\xc3\xb3n Ru\xc3\xadz">Ant\xc3\xb3n Ru\xc3\xadz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Punta_Santiago,_Humacao,_Puerto_Rico" title="Punta Santiago, Humacao, Puerto Rico">Punta Santiago</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Abajo,_Humacao,_Puerto_Rico" title="R\xc3\xado Abajo, Humacao, Puerto Rico">R\xc3\xado Abajo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buena_Vista,_Humacao,_Puerto_Rico" title="Buena Vista, Humacao, Puerto Rico">Buena Vista</a> and <a href="/wiki/Candelero_Abajo" title="Candelero Abajo">Candelero Abajo</a> barrios, are extremely vulnerable to flooding and destruction.<sup id="cite_ref-Quintana_END_Mitigation_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Quintana_END_Mitigation-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Barrios">Barrios</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Humacao,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Barrios"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Humacao,_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Humacao%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png/220px-Humacao%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="239" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Humacao%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png/330px-Humacao%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Humacao%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png/440px-Humacao%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png 2x" data-file-width="1100" data-file-height="1195" /></a><figcaption>Humacao map with barrio subdivisions</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Like all municipalities of Puerto Rico, Humacao is subdivided into <a href="/wiki/Barrios_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Barrios of Puerto Rico">barrios</a>. The municipal buildings, central square and large Catholic church are located in a small barrio referred to as <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">"el pueblo"</i></span>, near the center of the municipality.<sup id="cite_ref-Pico_1969_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pico_1969-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Law2015_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law2015-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-US2010Census_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US2010Census-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1184024115">.mw-parser-output .div-col{margin-top:0.3em;column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .div-col-small{font-size:90%}.mw-parser-output .div-col-rules{column-rule:1px solid #aaa}.mw-parser-output .div-col dl,.mw-parser-output .div-col ol,.mw-parser-output .div-col ul{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .div-col li,.mw-parser-output .div-col dd{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style><div class="div-col" style="column-width: 15em;">\n<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3n_Ru%C3%ADz" title="Ant\xc3\xb3n Ru\xc3\xadz">Ant\xc3\xb3n Ru\xc3\xadz</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Buena_Vista,_Humacao,_Puerto_Rico" title="Buena Vista, Humacao, Puerto Rico">Buena Vista</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Candelero_Abajo" title="Candelero Abajo">Candelero Abajo</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Candelero_Arriba" title="Candelero Arriba">Candelero Arriba</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Cata%C3%B1o,_Humacao,_Puerto_Rico" title="Cata\xc3\xb1o, Humacao, Puerto Rico">Cata\xc3\xb1o</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Collores,_Humacao,_Puerto_Rico" title="Collores, Humacao, Puerto Rico">Collores</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Humacao_barrio-pueblo" title="Humacao barrio-pueblo">Humacao barrio-pueblo</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mab%C3%BA" Rico">Mariana</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Punta_Santiago,_Humacao,_Puerto_Rico" title="Punta Santiago, Humacao, Puerto Rico">Punta Santiago</a></li>\n<li><a Puerto Rico">Tejas</a></li></ol>\n</div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sectors">Sectors</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Humacao,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Sectors"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Barrios (which are, in contemporary times, roughly comparable to <a href="/wiki/Minor_civil_divisions" class="mw-redirect" title="Minor civil divisions">minor civil divisions</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-Barrio-Pueblo_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barrio-Pueblo-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and subbarrios,<sup id="cite_ref-Census_map_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census_map-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> are further subdivided into smaller areas called <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">sectores</i></span> (<i>sectors</i> in English). The types of <i>sectores</i> may vary, from normally <i>sector</i> to <i>urbanizaci\xc3\xb3n</i> to <i>reparto</i> to <i>barriada</i> to <i>residencial</i>, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Law_1-2001_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law_1-2001-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Special_Communities">Special Communities</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Humacao,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Special Communities"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1236090951">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Office_for_Socioeconomic_and_Community_Development" title="Puerto Rico Office for Socioeconomic and Community Development">Puerto Rico Office for Socioeconomic and Community Development</a></div>\n<p><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Comunidades Especiales de Puerto Rico</i></span> (Special Communities of Puerto Rico) are marginalized communities whose citizens are experiencing a certain amount of <a href="/wiki/Social_exclusion" title="Social exclusion">social exclusion</a>. A map shows these communities occur in nearly every municipality of the commonwealth. Of the 742 places that were on the list in 2014, the following barrios, communities, sectors, or neighborhoods were in Humacao: Ant\xc3\xb3n Ruiz, Obrera neighborhood, Cotto Mab\xc3\xba-Fermina, Buena Vista, Parcelas Aniseto Cruz in Candelero Abajo, Parcelas Mart\xc3\xadnez in Candelero Abajo, Cata\xc3\xb1o, Punta Santiago, Verde Mar, and Cangrejos.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wordpress.com_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wordpress.com-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Demographics">Demographics</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Humacao,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Demographics"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1224496135">.mw-parser-output .us-census-pop{border-spacing:1px;border:1px solid #a2a9b1;background-color:var(--background-color-neutral-subtle,#f8f9fa);padding:0.3em;font-size:95%}.mw-parser-output .us-census-pop class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Tourism">Tourism</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Humacao,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Tourism"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>To stimulate local tourism, the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Tourism_Company" title="Puerto Rico Tourism Company">Puerto Rico Tourism Company</a> launched the <i>Voy Turistiendo</i> ("I\'m Touring") campaign, with a passport book and website. The Humacao page lists <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Reserva Natural de Humacao</i></span>, its <a href="/wiki/Humacao_barrio-pueblo" title="Humacao barrio-pueblo">Pueblo</a> with historic architecture, and its cuisine, specifically <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Granito</i></span>, as places and things of interest.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Palmasdelmarplaya.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Palmasdelmarplaya.JPG/200px-Palmasdelmarplaya.JPG" decoding="async" width="200" height="134" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Palmasdelmarplaya.JPG/300px-Palmasdelmarplaya.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Palmasdelmarplaya.JPG/400px-Palmasdelmarplaya.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a><figcaption>The beach at Palmas del Mar resort</figcaption></figure>\n<p>According to a news article by <a href="/wiki/Primera_Hora_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Primera Hora (Puerto Rico)">Primera Hora</a>, there are 8 beaches in Humacao including <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Punta Santiago</i></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Palmas del Mar</i></span> Beach in Humacao is considered a dangerous beach due to its strong currents.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Due to its location on the coast and relative short distance from the capital, Humacao is a frequent stop for tourists. One of the most notable tourist mainstays is the <a href="/wiki/Palmas_Del_Mar_Beach_Resort" class="mw-redirect" title="Palmas Del Mar Beach Resort">Palmas del Mar</a> resort, which is Puerto Rico\'s largest resort. This mega-resort is composed of over 3,000 acres (12&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) of land and occupies the entire southeastern portion of Humacao. The resort contains tennis courts, two world-class golf courses, beach access, several restaurants and a riding center.\n</p><p>Aside from the beaches at the Palmas del Mar resort, Humacao has other beaches. The most popular ones are <a href="/wiki/Punta_Santiago,_Humacao,_Puerto_Rico" title="Punta Santiago, Humacao, Puerto Rico">Punta Santiago</a>, Buena Vista, Punta Candelero, and El Morrillo.<sup id="cite_ref-enciclopediapr_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-enciclopediapr-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The Candelero Beach Resort, built in 1973, with its 107 rooms, 25 which are suites, was purchased and revitalized by the Suarez family.<sup id="cite_ref-END_Candelero_Beach_Resort_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-END_Candelero_Beach_Resort-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The Astronomical Observatory at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico_at_Humacao" title="University of Puerto Rico at Humacao">University of Puerto Rico at Humacao</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Casa_Roig" class="mw-redirect" title="Casa Roig">Casa Roig</a>, the Guzm\xc3\xa1n Ermit, the Humacao Wildlife Refuge, and the <a href="/wiki/Concatedral_Dulce_Nombre_de_Jes%C3%BAs_(Humacao,_Puerto_Rico)" title="Concatedral Dulce Nombre de Jes\xc3\xbas (Humacao, Puerto Rico)">Church Dulce Nombre de Jes\xc3\xbas</a> may be classed as other places of interest.\n</p><p>In the 1980s, the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Department_of_Natural_and_Environmental_Resources" title="Puerto Rico Department of Natural and Environmental Resources">Puerto Rico Department of Natural and Environmental Resources</a> established the <a href="/wiki/Humacao_Nature_Reserve" title="Humacao Nature Reserve">Humacao Nature Reserve</a> (also called the Punta Santiago Nature Reserve) in the municipality.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Palmas_del_Mar_Tropical_Forest" title="Palmas del Mar Tropical Forest">Palmas del Mar Tropical Forest</a> is also located in Humacao.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Economy">Economy</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Humacao,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Economy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Burlington_(department_store)" title="Burlington (department store)">Burlington</a> in Humacao employs under 100 people and reopened its doors in March 2019. The store had been shuttered since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a> destroyed it on September 19, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Culture">Culture</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Humacao,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Culture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Festivals_and_events">Festivals and events</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Humacao,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Festivals and events"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Humacao celebrates its <a href="/wiki/Fiestas_patronales_in_Puerto_Rico" title="Fiestas patronales in Puerto Rico">patron saint</a> festival in December. The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Fiestas Patronales Inmaculada Concepcion de Maria</i></span> is a religious and cultural celebration that generally features parades, games, artisans, amusement rides, regional food, and live entertainment.<sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Breadfruit" title="Breadfruit">Breadfruit</a> Festival</i> (<i>Festival de la Pana</i>) is celebrated during the first weekend of September. It is organized by the <i>Mariana\'s Recreational and Cultural Association</i> (ARECMA), a community organization of the Mariana barrio. Its main theme is about the preparation of dishes whose main ingredient is breadfruit. Typical Puerto Rican music, crafts and foods as well as other cultural and sports activities can also be enjoyed. Most years it has been held at one of the highest elevations within the sector with views to Humacao, <a href="/wiki/Las_Piedras,_Puerto_Rico" title="Las Piedras, Puerto Rico">Las Piedras</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naguabo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Naguabo, Puerto Rico">Naguabo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vieques" class="mw-redirect" title="Vieques">Vieques</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yabucoa" class="mw-redirect" title="Yabucoa">Yabucoa</a>.\n</p><p><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Humacao Grita</i></span> is an urban art festival held in November.<sup id="cite_ref-El_Foro_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-El_Foro-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Other festivals and events celebrated in Humacao include:<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Epiphany_(holiday)" title="Epiphany (holiday)">Three Kings\xe2\x80\x99 Day</a>- January</li>\n<li>Festival of the Cross \xe2\x80\x93 May</li>\n<li>Flat-bottom Boat Festival \xe2\x80\x93 June</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Saint_Cecilia" title="Saint Cecilia">Saint Cecilia</a> Festival (patron saint of musicians) \xe2\x80\x93 November</li>\n<li>Catholic Church Community Festival \xe2\x80\x93 December</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sports">Sports</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Humacao,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Sports"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The <i>Grises</i> basketball team (<i><a href="/wiki/Humacao_Grays" class="mw-redirect" title="Humacao Grays">Humacao Grays</a></i>), founded in 2005, belongs to Puerto Rico\'s <a href="/wiki/National_Superior_Basketball" class="mw-redirect" title="National Superior Basketball">National Superior Basketball</a> league. In 2010, they changed their name to the <a href="/wiki/Caciques_de_Humacao" title="Caciques de Humacao">Caciques de Humacao</a>. They play at the new <a href="/w/index.php?title=Humacao_Coliseum&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Humacao Coliseum (page does not exist)">Humacao Coliseum</a>.\n</p><p>The <i>Grises</i> is also a Double A class amateur baseball team that has won one championship (1951) and four time runners-up in (1950, 1960, 1965 and 1967).\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Government">Government</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Humacao,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Government"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mayoralty_in_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Mayoralty in Puerto Rico">Mayoralty in Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Humacao_District_Jail_in_Humacao,_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Humacao_District_Jail_in_Humacao%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/220px-Humacao_District_Jail_in_Humacao%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Humacao_District_Jail_in_Humacao%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/330px-Humacao_District_Jail_in_Humacao%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Humacao_District_Jail_in_Humacao%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/440px-Humacao_District_Jail_in_Humacao%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024" /></a><figcaption>Humacao District Jail</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Like all municipalities in <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, Humacao is administered by a mayor. In June 2022, Julio Geigel was elected mayor of Humacao.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Before then Luis Raul Sanchez got into office, after Marcelo Trujillo Panisse died in September 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-2019_mayor_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2019_mayor-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The former mayor was <a href="/wiki/Marcelo_Trujillo" title="Marcelo Trujillo">Marcelo Trujillo</a>, of the <a href="/wiki/Popular_Democratic_Party_of_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Popular Democratic Party of Puerto Rico">Popular Democratic Party</a> (PPD) was elected at the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_general_election,_2000" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rican general election, 2000">2000 general election</a> and served for many years. In the 2020 general election Luis Raul was defeated by Reinaldo (Rey) Vargas Rodr\xc3\xadguez (PNP) by a margin of 4 points.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, on May 5, 2022, Vargas was arrested by the <a href="/wiki/FBI" class="mw-redirect" title="FBI">FBI</a> on corruption, bribery, and extortion charges.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and was subsequently removed from his position.\n</p><p>The city belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Senatorial_district_VII" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rico Senatorial district VII">Puerto Rico Senatorial district VII</a>, which is represented by two Senators. In 2012, <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Su%C3%A1rez_C%C3%A1ceres" title="Jorge Su\xc3\xa1rez C\xc3\xa1ceres">Jorge Su\xc3\xa1rez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Dalmau" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Luis Dalmau">Jos\xc3\xa9 Luis Dalmau</a> were elected as District Senators.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="FBI_satellite_office">FBI satellite office</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Humacao,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: FBI satellite office"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>There is an <a href="/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation" title="Federal Bureau of Investigation">FBI</a> satellite office located in Humacao.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Healthcare">Healthcare</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Humacao,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Healthcare"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Humacao has three secondary care hospitals HIMA-San Pablo Humacao, Dr. Dom\xc3\xadnguez (Hospital Oriente), and Ryder Memorial Hospital.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Symbols">Symbols</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Humacao,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Symbols"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">municipio</i></span> has an official flag and coat of arms.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Flag">Flag</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Humacao,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Flag"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>It consists of three horizontal stripes: gold that stands for Chief Jumacao\'s crown, red that symbolizes the coat of arms and the green that represents the arrows used by the Ta\xc3\xadnos.<sup id="cite_ref-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Coat_of_arms">Coat of arms</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Humacao,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Coat of arms"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The coat of arms mainly consists of two colors, gold and green but also has gules. The gold represents the sun, Humacao is located in the island were the sun rises. Green symbolizes the native Indian heritage as well as the natural tropical valley where the city is located. The shield itself represents Humacao\'s native and Indian name origin. The coat of arms was designed by Roberto Brascochea Lota in 1975 and approved by Humacao on November 13, 1975.<sup id="cite_ref-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Transportation">Transportation</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Humacao,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Transportation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Humacao_airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Humacao airport">Humacao\'s airport</a> is no longer used for daily flights to <a href="/wiki/Vieques,_Puerto_Rico" title="Vieques, Puerto Rico">Vieques</a> and <a href="/wiki/Culebra,_Puerto_Rico" title="Culebra, Puerto Rico">Culebra</a> as it was in the past. It is now used for private flights.\n</p><p>Humacao is served by two freeways and one tolled expressway, therefore is one of a few cities in Puerto Rico with good access. <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_30" title="Puerto Rico Highway 30">Puerto Rico Highway 30</a>, <i><b>Autopista Cruz Ortiz Stella</b></i>, serves as the main highway coming from the west (<a href="/wiki/Caguas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Caguas, Puerto Rico">Caguas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Las_Piedras,_Puerto_Rico" title="Las Piedras, Puerto Rico">Las Piedras</a>), while <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_53" title="Puerto Rico Highway 53">Puerto Rico Highway 53</a> serves from the north (<a href="/wiki/Fajardo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Fajardo, Puerto Rico">Fajardo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naguabo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Naguabo, Puerto Rico">Naguabo</a>) and south (<a href="/wiki/Yabucoa,_Puerto_Rico" title="Yabucoa, Puerto Rico">Yabucoa</a>). <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_60" title="Puerto Rico Highway 60">Puerto Rico Highway 60</a>, the <i><b>Carretera Dionisio Casillas</b></i>, is a short freeway located entirely in Humacao, and has exits serving <a href="/wiki/Humacao_barrio-pueblo" title="Humacao barrio-pueblo">downtown Humacao</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3n_Ru%C3%ADz" title="Ant\xc3\xb3n Ru\xc3\xadz">Anton Ruiz</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_3" title="Puerto Rico Highway 3">Puerto Rico Highway 3</a>, the main highway bordering the east coastline of Puerto Rico from <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a>, passes through Humacao and has its only alt route in the town, known locally as the <i>Bulevar del Rio</i> (River Boulevard) where it has access to the main judiciary center of the city, as well as a future theatre that is being built, the <i><b>Centro de Bellas Artes de Humacao</b></i> (Humacao Fine Arts Center). The alt route allows people to pass by the downtown area, as PR-3 enters into the downtown and business center of the town.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_908" title="Puerto Rico Highway 908">Puerto Rico Highway 908</a> is another important highway, which begins at <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_3" title="Puerto Rico Highway 3">PR-3</a> and intersects <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_30" title="Puerto Rico Highway 30">PR-30</a> and has access to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico_at_Humacao" title="University of Puerto Rico at Humacao">University of Puerto Rico at Humacao</a>, as well as some main schools in the municipality.\n</p><p>Humacao, together with San Juan and <a href="/wiki/Salinas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Salinas, Puerto Rico">Salinas</a>, is one of three municipalities in Puerto Rico that has <a href="/wiki/Controlled-access_highway" title="Controlled-access highway">controlled-access highways</a> leaving its boundaries in all directions (in this case north to <a href="/wiki/Naguabo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Naguabo, Puerto Rico">Naguabo</a> and south to <a href="/wiki/Yabucoa,_Puerto_Rico" title="Yabucoa, Puerto Rico">Yabucoa</a> via <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_53" title="Puerto Rico Highway 53">PR-53</a> and west to Las Piedras via PR-30)\n</p><p>There are 68 bridges in Humacao.<sup id="cite_ref-bridge_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bridge-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Education">Education</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Humacao,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Education"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>There are various elementary and high school facilities, three of which were recognized by the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Middle_States_Association_of_Secondary_Schools&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Middle States Association of Secondary Schools (page does not exist)">Middle States Association of Secondary Schools</a> and each has its own <a href="/wiki/National_Honor_Society" title="National Honor Society">National Honor Society</a> chapters. These include Colegio San Antonio Abad, founded in 1957 and operated by the <a href="/wiki/Benedictine" class="mw-redirect" title="Benedictine">Benedictine</a> <a href="/wiki/Monk" title="Monk">monks</a> of the Abad\xc3\xada San Antonio Abad.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico_at_Humacao" title="University of Puerto Rico at Humacao">University of Puerto Rico at Humacao</a>, formerly the CUH, educates over 4,000 students and is well known for its sciences, producing many of the island\'s most skilled microbiologists, marine biologists, wildlife biologists and chemists at the undergraduate level. It also manages an astronomical observatory where many tourists and locals come visit and view the stars and planets and the <i>Museo Casa Roig</i> where arts expositions and cultural events are celebrated.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Notable_natives_and_residents">Notable natives and residents</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Humacao,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Notable natives and residents"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:People_from_Humacao,_Puerto_Rico" title="Category:People from Humacao, Puerto Rico">Category:People from Humacao, Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Rita_Moreno" title="Rita Moreno">Rita Moreno</a>, Academy Award-winning actress</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Edwin_N%C3%BA%C3%B1ez" title="Edwin N\xc3\xba\xc3\xb1ez">Edwin N\xc3\xba\xc3\xb1ez</a>, professional baseball player</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Luis_Rafael_S%C3%A1nchez" title="Luis Rafael S\xc3\xa1nchez">Luis Rafael S\xc3\xa1nchez</a>, novelist and author</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Rossana_Rodriguez-Sanchez" title="Rossana Rodriguez-Sanchez">Rossana Rodriguez-Sanchez</a>, member of the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_City_Council" title="Chicago City Council">Chicago City Council</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Eddie_Mir%C3%B3" title="Eddie Mir\xc3\xb3">Eddie Mir\xc3\xb3</a>, TV personality</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Julio_M._Fuentes" title="Julio M. Fuentes">Julio M. Fuentes</a>, US Circuit Court judge</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tito_Rojas" title="Tito Rojas">Tito Rojas</a>, salsa singer</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Adamari_L%C3%B3pez" title="Adamari L\xc3\xb3pez">Adamari L\xc3\xb3pez</a>, actress</li>\n<li>Papulin Moyett, periodista y locutor de radio</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Jaquira_D%C3%ADaz" title="Jaquira D\xc3\xadaz">Jaquira D\xc3\xadaz</a>, author, journalist</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Cosculluela" title="Cosculluela">Cosculluela</a>, rapper, songwriter</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Eladio_Carri%C3%B3n" title="Eladio Carri\xc3\xb3n">Eladio Carri\xc3\xb3n</a>, rapper, songwriter</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Jumacao" title="Jumacao">Jumacao</a>, Taino Cacique</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Benito_Pastoriza_Iyodo" title="Benito Pastoriza Iyodo">Benito Pastoriza Iyodo</a>, poet, narrator, and essayist</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Carlos_Ponce" title="Carlos Ponce">Carlos Ponce</a>, actor</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Luis_Antonio_Rivera" title="Luis Antonio Rivera">Luis Antonio "Yoyo Boing" Rivera</a>, actor and comedian</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Diplo" title="Diplo">Diplo</a>,comedian</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Jerry_Rivera"
